   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiceless postalveolar affricate
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

      </a>
      )
     </span>

      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiceless palato-alveolar sibilant affricate
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        voiceless domed postalveolar sibilant affricate
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_communication" title="Speech communication">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The sound is transcribed in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       with ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t͡ʃ
       </span>
       ⟩, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t͜ʃ
       </span>
       ⟩ or ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        tʃ
       </span>
       ⟩ (formerly the ligature ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ʧ
       </span>
       ⟩). It is familiar to English speakers as the "ch" sound in "chip".
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, this sound often derives from a former
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_stop" title="Voiceless velar stop">
        voiceless velar stop
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /k/
       </span>
       (as in
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Arabic" title="Gulf Arabic">
        Gulf Arabic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
        Slavic languages
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranian_languages" title="Indo-Iranian languages">
        Indo-Iranian languages
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       ), or a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_stop" title="Voiceless dental stop">
        voiceless dental stop
       </a>
       by way of palatalization, especially next to a
       <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">
        front vowel
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiceless domed postalveolar affricate:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">
         sibilant
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">
         affricate
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by first stopping the air flow entirely, then directing it with the tongue to the sharp edge of the teeth, causing high-frequency
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulence
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Palato-alveolar_consonant" title="Palato-alveolar consonant">
          palato-alveolar
         </a>
        </i>
        , that is, domed (partially
        <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">
         palatalized
        </a>
        )
        <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
         postalveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the blade of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue" title="Tongue">
         tongue
        </a>
        behind the
        <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
         alveolar ridge
        </a>
        , and the front of the tongue bunched up ("domed") at the
        <a href="/wiki/Palate" title="Palate">
         palate
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>

            </b>

           </a>

         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [pɾe̞ˈzẽ̞t͡ʃi]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'present'
        </td>
        <td>
         Allophone of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /
          <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Dental_or_denti-alveolar" title="Voiceless dental and alveolar stops">
           t
          </a>
          /
         </span>
         before
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /i, ĩ/
         </span>
         (including when
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [i, ĩ, j]
         </span>
         is not actually produced) and other instances of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [i]
         </span>
         (e.g.
         <a href="/wiki/Epenthesis#Epenthesis_of_a_vowel,_or_anaptyxis" title="Epenthesis">
          epenthesis
         </a>
         ), marginal sound otherwise. See
         <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_phonology" title="Portuguese phonology">
          Portuguese phonology
         </a>
        </td>

      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">
        Mandarin Chinese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">
        Korean
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
        Polish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">
        Thai
       </a>
       have a
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal affricate">
        voiceless alveolo-palatal affricate
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /t͡ɕ/
       </span>
       ; this is technically postalveolar but it is less precise to use
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /t͡ʃ/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voiceless_postalveolar_non-sibilant_affricate">
        Voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant affricate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Voiceless postalveolar non-sibilant affricate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>

           t̠͡ɹ̠̊˔
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_2">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">
         affricate
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by first stopping the airflow entirely, then allowing air flow through a constricted channel at the place of articulation, causing turbulence.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
         postalveolar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue behind the alveolar ridge.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence_2">
        Occurrence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Occurrence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         Language
        </th>

        <td rowspan="4">
         <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
          English
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Australian_English" title="Australian English">
          Australian
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoxFletcher2017144_15-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoxFletcher2017144-15">
           [15]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="4">
         <span lang="en">
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/English_alphabet" title="English alphabet">
            <b>
             tr
            </b>
            ee
           </a>
          </i>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="3">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [t̠ɹ̠̊˔ʷɪi̯]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="4">
         'tree'
        </td>
        <td rowspan="4">
         Phonetic realization of the stressed, syllable-initial sequence
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /tr/
         </span>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoxFletcher2017144_15-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoxFletcher2017144-15">
           [15]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGimson2014177,_186–188,_192_16-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGimson2014177,_186–188,_192-16">
           [16]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWells2008_17-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWells2008-17">
           [17]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConnolly1990121_18-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConnolly1990121-18">
           [18]
          </a>
         </sup>
         In General American and Received Pronunciation, the less common alternative is alveolar
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_non-sibilant_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar non-sibilant affricate">
           tɹ̝̊
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGimson2014177,_186–188,_192_16-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGimson2014177,_186–188,_192-16">
           [16]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Australian_English_phonology" title="Australian English phonology">
          Australian English phonology
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/English_phonology" title="English phonology">
          English phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/General_American" title="General American">
          General American
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGimson2014177,_186–188,_192_16-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGimson2014177,_186–188,_192-16">
           [16]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWells2008_17-1">

           [17]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
